The Press Conference in Warsaw: Fifth Letter from Poland – Special Correspondent Mao Shuqing of This Newspaper

During my journey in Warsaw, what I admired and appreciated the most was the Polish International Publicity Department, or "Polish Publicity Department," which belongs to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and is equivalent to many "departments" in rank. The director, Grot, is a middle-aged man with a receding hairline who speaks fluent English and Russian effortlessly. Some say he is proficient in six languages; at the very least, I know his French is also excellent. People in the Polish Ministry of Foreign Affairs call him "General." It is said that he once served in the military for a while, but he is essentially a man of letters. Since the restoration, he has been burdened with the most "important" work of the Polish government.

Grot holds three foreign press conferences every week, at twelve noon on Mondays, Wednesdays, and Fridays. Each meeting is a debate with sharp tongues and swords. I truly admire those British and American colleagues who have such sharp questions, but General Grot is always able to handle them with ease. I remember during one particular week in Warsaw, all three press conferences discussed the issue of American aid for European food. Marshall, in Washington, based on Harrison's report, said that Poland had more than enough food and did not need further American aid. At the press conference, Wan Luo protested strongly on behalf of the government, calling Harrison's report a "lie" and Marshall's decision "unfair."

He always speaks in English first, then translates himself into Russian. At foreign press conferences, English and Russian are considered official languages. Journalists from Czechoslovakia, Yugoslavia, and the Soviet Union appreciate his Russian, while we feel his English is really beautiful. Due to differences in language and political background, the same round table is invisibly divided into two camps. What I find most interesting is the cigarettes on the table. Chinese, British, American, and French journalists all smoke American cigarettes, while journalists from Russia, Czechoslovakia, South [Yugoslavia], Finland, etc., all smoke Russian cigarettes.

The first time I attended a foreign press conference, many British and American journalists looked at me but did not speak to me. I remember very clearly that it was not until I took out a pack of "Marquis" cigarettes from my pocket and placed it on the table that an American female journalist leaned over and started talking to me.

However, General Wan Luo is able to deal with both sides very well. Firstly, his linguistic talent allows him to move easily between all parties. Secondly, he possesses rich knowledge and a quick mind. When protesting Harrison's report, he particularly emphasized that Poland's summer and autumn crops this year lacked seeds and provided many figures to support his claim. An American journalist said, "May I ask why the Polish government doesn't get seeds from Russia and always asks the United States?" The tone of the question was clearly humorous, what they call "digging" in Shanghai dialect, but Wan Luo remained calm. He said, "From Russia? We are currently negotiating in Moscow; whether it succeeds or not is another matter." He went on to say, "There are rich countries in the world and there are poor countries. Russia and the United States were both allies of Poland during the war. It would not be reasonable for us not to ask the United States but instead to ask Russia, which is preoccupied with its own problems. And as for the United States, it would be unfair to favor one ally over another!"

The second time the food issue was discussed, Grot invited a government official in charge of farming and import-export trade to report. The conclusion, of course, was still to criticize the United States for its "bias and unfairness." A journalist named Wheeler from the Chicago Daily News, who had just arrived from the United States, was so enraged that he stood up and said angrily, "During the war, the United States spent so much money and so many lives to liberate many European countries. After the war, the United States continues to spend tens of billions of dollars to help the Allies. May I ask what offense has Poland suffered to warrant such harsh criticism?" Grot smiled and told him, "You must have just come from the United States, sir. You didn't hear the first part. What you said is correct, but it's not the issue being discussed now. I'm sorry, please be quiet!"

Grot is a loyal Polish Communist, which his female secretary, Anna Krzysztof, told me when I hosted her for dinner. I stuck out my tongue, and she asked why. I said, "I am a professional journalist, and Grot is in the same line of work. From the perspective of my peers, I believe that a top-notch Polish talent like him should be above any partisan prejudice." I repeated, "I regret his joining the Communist Party."

Partisan bias can hinder the truthfulness of news reports. I remember at one meeting discussing the food issue, a British journalist asked, "May I ask if Poland has any intention of sending its food out the back door to another country and then requesting aid from the United States through the front door?" Grot replied, "No." Then, another American female journalist asked, "Can you guarantee that?" Grot hesitated for a moment and still said, "I guarantee with my conscience that there is absolutely no such thing!"

I plan to introduce the general situation of Polish industry and agriculture in future dispatches. Here, I should point out that the iron discipline of the Communist Party is clearly reflected in Poland. Several weeks before I arrived in Warsaw, when Marshall gave a speech at Harvard University about the European Economic Recovery Plan, the Polish government and public, especially most of the leftist newspapers, had loudly touted their "sincere support" and warm welcome. The day Molotov flew to Paris was almost the happiest day for the Polish intellectuals. There are two reasons to explain this: first, Poland's devastated situation meant they hoped to use the Marshall Plan to achieve economic reconstruction. Second, and more importantly, the Polish people hoped that the Marshall Plan could invisibly eliminate the division between Eastern and Western Europe and bridge the gap between the Soviet bloc and the British-American bloc.

However, Molotov's short trip to Paris shattered their dreams. Non-communist Polish intellectuals once again fell into the dark abyss, anxiously envisioning a bleak future and a difficult situation. The Communist left-wing newspapers made a 180-degree turn and criticized the Marshall Plan, using satirical and sharp headlines to say that Marshall was boldly fooling the European people. (To be continued).

Qingdao U.S. Military Incident: Sino-American Consultation to Remedy

[Qingdao Dispatch from Our Newspaper, 28th] Major Ogg, the commander of the U.S. Marine Corps military police stationed in Qingdao, recently discussed several remedial measures with the Chinese authorities regarding the continuous incidents caused by the U.S. military: U.S. soldiers guarding will use shotguns, but may still shoot when necessary; however, shotguns are not lethal beyond four steps. For those who attempt to escape after causing traffic accidents, all U.S. military police patrol cars will now be equipped with wireless telephones for communication and command, which can quickly intercept the culprit drivers and severely punish them. To avoid U.S. soldiers mistakenly taking private cars for taxis and forcing rides, the two types of vehicles will now be marked with separate signs for clarification. The placing of "Out of Bounds" signs by the U.S. military in various bars, which infringes upon Chinese sovereignty, is something Major Ogg insists on; the matter is now being referred to Mayor Li and Commander Kirk for resolution. In the event of an incident, doctors from both China and the United States should be present for examination.

Editorial

Refuting Stryker's Argument Against Reparations

Mr. Stryker, advisor on reparations issues for the U.S. Department of the Army, recently published an article in "America Magazine" entitled "Retaliation is Waste," fundamentally opposing the United Nations' demands for reparations from Germany and Japan. Regarding the issue of Japanese reparations, he even advocated abandoning the Pauley mission's reparations plan and overturning the Far Eastern Commission's resolutions on this issue, so that Japan could retain a higher level of industry and embark on a path of self-sufficiency. When we saw Mr. Stryker's argument against reparations, we initially thought that this was merely Mr. Stryker's personal opinion and could not represent the attitude of the American diplomatic authorities towards the issue of Japanese reparations, and therefore did not deserve much attention. However, based on Mr. Stryker's brief biography, he has served as an advisor on reparations issues for the U.S. Department of the Army since November 1945, worked in Germany for a year, and then returned to the United States, where he served as chairman of the Special Committee on Japanese Reparations and represented the Department of the Army in investigating the situation in Japan. Now, he has published such a strange argument against reparations, which is indeed worthy of our attention. Moreover, this strange argument can be mutually confirmed with the delayed attitude of the Allied Headquarters in Tokyo towards the issue of reparations. Especially in the United States, after an individual's views are published in newspapers and magazines, if they can gain the approval of the majority of the people, then they can influence American policy towards Japan. Therefore, Mr. Stryker's publication of the argument against reparations will have an adverse impact on the Allies' demands for reparations, which deserves the attention of our country's government and public.

We have repeatedly read Mr. Stryker's article published in "America Magazine" and summarized the main points as follows: The United States does not need the industrial equipment of Germany and Japan, so the United States not only does not want reparations from Germany and Japan, but should also encourage or help Germany and Japan to be self-sufficient. Only in this way can the United States stop its relief efforts. Regarding the issue of reparations from Germany, the opinions of Britain and the United States are relatively close, both advocating giving Germany a better opportunity to produce more food and more goods that can be exported. However, the Soviet Union demanded 10 billion U.S. dollars in reparations from Germany, and France also wanted to collect as much as possible from Germany, which were both opposed by the United States. The Pauley plan has been approved by the Far Eastern Commission, and the U.S. representative has also expressed agreement, but the United States should abandon or revise this plan. China and the Soviet Union can both exercise veto power within the Far Eastern Commission and will inevitably express objections to the United States' revision of the Pauley plan. In order to implement its demands, the United States has no choice but to set aside the Far Eastern Commission. Even if the eventual outcome is the United States making peace with Japan alone, it is worth doing.

If we stand in the narrow, selfish position of the American people to read Mr. Stryker's grand argument, we may also think that it is reasonable. But from our perspective, Mr. Stryker's fallacies, if adopted by the American authorities, will not only mislead people and have an adverse impact on other countries, but will also inevitably lead to the United States suffering the consequences and making a major diplomatic mistake.

First, during the occupation, the United States certainly spent a large number of U.S. dollars in Germany and Japan, which the American taxpayers had to bear. However, the purpose of occupying Germany and Japan was to control them, to disarm them militarily, to make them increasingly democratic politically, and to reduce their industrial level economically, thereby fundamentally eliminating their aggressive ideology and depriving them of their aggressive strength, so as not to launch another world war. Therefore, the burden on American taxpayers today can be said to be the price of permanent peace, and certainly not a waste. The meaning of reparations is not only to punish the defeated countries, but also to thoroughly destroy their war industries so that their aggressive train cannot start again. Reparations are not about retaliation, let alone waste. It is true that the United States does not need the industrial equipment of Germany and Japan, but this certainly cannot be used as a reason to oppose reparations, nor can it be used as a reason to prevent other victorious countries from dismantling German and Japanese factories, let alone encourage and help the defeated countries maintain their industrial level, so that their aggressive ambitions will not be rekindled one day.

Second, in recent years, the Allied Headquarters has consistently adopted a lenient attitude towards Japan. This newspaper has repeatedly written articles believing that leniency is sufficient to breed evil, and special vigilance should be raised regarding Japan's rapid recovery. Mr. Stryker's views are completely the same as what the Allied Headquarters has done. Therefore, we cannot help but suspect that some people in the United States today have gradually forgotten the painful lessons of the Pearl Harbor incident, and in the minds of these people, the enemy of the United States in the Far East is no longer Japan, and in Europe it is no longer Germany. The formation of this kind of thinking is really too dangerous! Not only is it enough to promote the division of the world at present, but it is also enough to lead to another war in the future. Judging from the diplomatic offensive that the United States has adopted at the Second General Assembly of the United Nations, it can be seen that the United States is moving along this road.

Third, the Far Eastern Commission was created in accordance with the Moscow Three-Power Foreign Ministers Conference Declaration, and its sole task is to deal with the Japanese problem and draft a peace treaty with Japan. Because China, Britain, the United States, and the Soviet Union are the countries most closely related to the Far Eastern situation, they all have the special privilege of veto power. The existence of veto power is certainly sufficient to hinder the progress of the Far Eastern Commission, but for the sake of a fair and lasting peace in the Far East, the veto power should be retained, and at most it can only be restricted. The United States wants to set aside the Far Eastern Commission, and there is ultimately no legal basis for it in the process of drafting a peace treaty with Japan. Moreover, once the steps are disrupted, drafting a peace treaty with Japan will become more difficult.

Fourth, the idea of the United States making peace with Germany and Japan alone was first advocated by former President Hoover. Although American public opinion was interested in it, the American government did not pay much attention to it. Today, seeing Mr. Stryker's strange argument, he also advocates making peace alone, which shows that Hoover's advocacy has gradually become more common and powerful in the United States today. However, it must be known that peace is indivisible. If the United States truly wants to make peace with Japan alone, it is meaningless and will only cause international disputes.

In short, American policy towards Japan seems to need to be changed. We want to advise the American diplomatic authorities not to haggle over their own immediate interests, but to plan for the entire Far East.

Weekly Forum

Political Reform and the Talent Problem (Part 2)

— Du Zuozhou

Naturally, it cannot be said that all true talents are abandoned or misplaced, without obtaining appropriate positions. But under the current severe economic situation and meager treatment, the income of a senior civil servant or university professor is almost less than that of a rickshaw puller. Those who remain steadfast and self-disciplined have no choice but to endure hunger and cold, and wait for death; while those with wavering wills, on the contrary, have many ways to gain both fame and fortune. Zeng Guofan, grieving over the politics of his time, once said with deep sorrow: "Everyone thinks that the lack of soldiers is not enough to be deeply worried about today, and the lack of salaries is not enough to weep bitterly over, but looking around this world, it is impossible to find someone who does not put personal gain first and fears being behind in rushing to righteousness, and who is filled with loneliness and indignation; or even if such a person is found, he is forced to live in a humble position until he is old, sick, frustrated, leaves, or dies, while those who are greedy and cowardly are promoted to the top, and become rich, famous, healthy, and immortal—is this something to be celebrated!" These words are no different from a portrayal of today's situation. How similar the societal distress and the mistreatment of talent are between then and now!

We want to shout out that to reform politics, we must first pay attention to the talent problem, that is, to pay attention to the way out for intellectuals in general. Intellectuals, appearing in Chinese history as scholar-officials, have a special status and influence, and the heirloom of successive rulers has been to rack their brains to win over and control intellectuals. In today's democratic era, those who hold power can no longer copy the control policies of the past, but if they are not even as good as the shallow techniques of treating scholar-officials in the past, then when will the source of national chaos be eliminated? It is a thought-provoking question.

Solving the talent problem naturally starts with education, but distant water cannot quench immediate thirst. The country has been running education for decades, and today we have such a serious talent problem. This is certainly not the fault of education itself, but rather than placing hope in the effects of the distant future, why not find ways to settle and properly arrange the talents that have already been cultivated? Moreover, solving the talent problem of this generation is tantamount to opening up a bright path for the talent cultivation of the next generation. Otherwise, if talents are wasted generation after generation, what can be imagined for the future of the country and the nation?

Finally, regarding the solution to the talent problem, which depends on the proper way to maintain talent, the author believes that the following points should be thoroughly implemented:

Loosen the restrictions on qualifications: We admit that qualifications such as diplomas and letters of appointment are standards for measuring talent, but overly emphasizing qualifications is like "judging people by appearance and losing sight of Ziyu," because "appearance" is formal, and qualifications are also formal. True talents do not necessarily have qualifications, and those with qualifications are not necessarily all talents. Strict civil service systems can only deal with ordinary talents and prevent the evils of speculation and good fortune, but for special and outstanding talents, they must be promoted exceptionally so that they can fully display their talents without being bound by the restrictions of qualifications.

Eliminate unworthy officials: "When owls are in the forest, phoenixes flee." If mediocrity is not removed, talent will not come. From ancient times, petty people and gentlemen cannot work together. Therefore, if the authorities have the determination to use new people and implement new policies, they must first eliminate the old and unworthy elements, and then new people can be introduced, and true talents will be happy to serve. Rectifying officialdom and cleaning up the bureaucracy is the first priority.

Open up more avenues for employing people: The state's formal way of recruiting talents is through examinations. Dr. Sun Yat-sen advocated the examination system and listed it as one of the five powers, which was truly a brilliant insight. However, the past national college entrance examinations and various special examinations have only served as embellishments, a "spot of red in a sea of green," and have not been able to have an impact on the entire system. In the future, in order to open up more avenues for employing people and give talents the opportunity to "stand out," it is most appropriate to strengthen the implementation of the examination system. In addition, investigating unemployment, conducting talent registration, and providing job placement services are also very important.

Straighten out the discipline of elections: Elections are the first step into politics, and campaigning is an opportunity for talents to demonstrate themselves. How cautiously should this be held in the grand ceremony of opening the country. However, the current election discipline is too disappointing. Campaigning involves collusion and spending hundreds of millions at every turn; fights and disturbances are even recorded in the newspapers from time to time. This has simply become a competition of money and force, what does it have to do with talent! In order to protect the sanctity of politics, we cannot help but call out the slogan of "straightening out election discipline" to urge attention from all parties!

Increase the remuneration at all levels: This goes without saying. But like the standard for adjusting the remuneration of civil servants that the Executive Yuan passed this time, increasing the basic allowance by "100,000 yuan" per person, as the professors at Peking University said: "It's simply joking with us!" If we continue to "joke" like this, talents will either be gone or starve to death, how can this be!

In short, to reform politics, we must first pay attention to solving the talent problem. As the saying goes, "cadres determine everything," that is, talents determine everything. We hope that the government can be decisive in personnel renewal and truly show a refreshing appearance. This is really the key to whether our politics can be thoroughly reformed. Throughout history, politicians who have molded and shaped the talents of an era have certainly not been able to avoid lamenting the existence of "pearls buried in the sea," but their attitude of cherishing talent like life and treating the virtuous with courtesy can inspire the common people, and "all around will dare not disobey." Therefore, the principles of employing people and administering government are actually very simple. If they are understood with divine clarity, then all rivers will flow into the sea, and all the talents in the world will be used for one's own benefit; if they are acted against, then there will be collapse and overflow, and there will be no way to clean up the mess. The complexity of the talent problem is such!

Save the domestic talents who are in distress! "As long as the green hills remain, there is no fear of running out of firewood." Talents are the country's "green hills." We must cherish them and protect them. The future of national construction really depends on them. (The End)

Promoting Korean Political Independence Should be Monitored by the United Nations; US Stance on Korean Issue is Clear; Likely to Largely Agree with Soviet Withdrawal Proposal

[United Press International, Washington, 28th] US officials feel they have achieved some real progress in resolving the Korean issue. Sources with inside knowledge say the US is expected to issue a statement next week welcoming the Soviet proposal for the joint withdrawal of US and Soviet troops from Korea. At the same time, the US will intensify its call for the UN General Assembly to consider the issue of Korean independence under a unified government. If the current plan can be thoroughly implemented, the US will indirectly point out that the Soviet proposal, in fact, accepts one of the seven points the US advocated on August 28th, which the Soviets then rejected. At that time, the US requested a four-power conference on Korea and stated its views on the purpose of this conference. The US requested immediate elections of legislative representatives in the US and Soviet occupation zones, the creation of a constitution for Korea under UN supervision, and the US hoped that the provisional government of Korea and related countries could agree on a date for the withdrawal of occupying forces from Korea. In addition, the US suggested in August that all steps of this plan be monitored by the United Nations and that allied nations jointly decide on the economic assistance Korea should receive. While accepting the Soviet withdrawal proposal, the US will insist that UN personnel be dispatched to supervise the withdrawal and election process to prevent conspiracies that might be launched by extreme reactionary elements in the US-occupied zone and communist cells in the Soviet-occupied zone. General opinion here is that the Soviet Union's sudden tacit approval of a portion of the US plan may accelerate agreement on Korean independence, but it may also deprive Korea of much of the economic assistance it could obtain from the US. The US intends to use the continuation of the US-Soviet stalemate to force Congress to agree to allocate long-term aid to Korea. If the Soviet Union suddenly agrees to withdraw and agrees to UN supervision of Korea, it is generally believed that interest here in economic assistance may decrease as a result. In any case, the US representative in the UN will seek ways to make the allied nations economically responsible for Korea and will point out the necessary construction while ensuring the maximum cooperation of the US to promote this matter.

[United Press, Seoul, 28th] It was learned today that the Soviet Union's recent proposal for the simultaneous withdrawal of US and Soviet occupying forces from Korea next spring contained the phrase "believing that this withdrawal will give the Korean people the opportunity to organize their own government with the assistance of allied nations." After being translated by American experts, it was mistakenly interpreted as "will give the Korean people the opportunity to organize their own government without relying on the assistance of allied nations." This led to statements by Korean leaders such as Syngman Rhee, who believed that as a result, Korea would be in danger of civil war.

Vyshinsky Discusses the Korean Issue; Advocates Consultation Among Three Powers; Opposes Submitting the Issue to the UN General Assembly

[Central News Agency, Lake Success, 27th] Soviet Deputy Foreign Minister Vyshinsky issued a statement on the Korean issue at a press conference yesterday. The full text is as follows: He said that the Korean issue should be resolved through an agreement between the Soviet Union, Britain, and the United States. A reporter asked what the prospects were for resolving the Korean issue within the UN General Assembly. He replied that his view was optimistic, and he believed that if one wanted to resolve this issue, one needed to take a small step, which was to withdraw this issue from the UN agenda. The UN General Assembly, in any case, has no reason to discuss this issue; it should be resolved by an agreement among the three powers that have certain obligations regarding this issue, namely the Soviet Union, Britain, and the United States.

We are deeply aware that it is the United States' suggestion to abolish the negotiations of the US-Soviet Joint Commission and deny the need to immediately grant Korea independence. What I want to say on this matter is that the Soviet delegation, in its statement opposing the Korean issue being submitted to the UN General Assembly, stated that the best way to resolve this issue was to resolve it without the participation of the General Assembly. He also solemnly pointed out that the fact is that this issue is not within the capacity of the UN General Assembly and involves Article 11 of the Charter, which also involves the obligations and provisions of the agreement reached at the 1945 Moscow Foreign Ministers Conference, which are truly needed to resolve the second paragraph of Article 37 regarding the Korean issue. I can also quote what was said by a United Press reporter and several other reports to implement the proposal of General Shtykov, the chief Soviet representative to the US-Soviet Joint Commission, which advocated that the US and Soviet occupying forces in Korea withdraw simultaneously from Korea in early 1948 and that the future issues be left to the Korean people to decide for themselves. All I can say is that we believe this is the best way to resolve this issue and the Korean issue. In order to help resolve this issue, we should remove it from the UN General Assembly agenda. Note by the reporter: Vyshinsky's statement did not mention China, which is deeply noteworthy.

The Soviet Union Presents a Counterproposal on the Greek Issue to the UN General Assembly; Demands that Foreign Troops Withdraw from Greek Territory

[Reuters, Lake Success, New York, 27th] Soviet Representative Gromyko presented a new resolution to the UN General Assembly's Political Committee, accusing Greece of being fully responsible for all border incidents and demanding that foreign troops withdraw from Greece and that a special committee be established to supervise foreign aid to Greece. The resolution stated: The Greek authorities should bear full responsibility for the border incidents between Greece and Yugoslavia, Bulgaria, and Albania; The internal situation in Greece is the main reason for the border tensions; The current situation in Greece is largely due to foreign interference in Greece's internal affairs.

The resolution also called on the UN General Assembly to make the following recommendations: The Greek government should take measures to prevent border incidents; Greece should restore normal relations with its neighbors; Greece, Bulgaria, Yugoslavia, and Albania should conclude new border conventions and resolve the refugee problem; The Greek government should take measures to stop discrimination against Macedonian and Albanian citizens; Withdraw foreign troops stationed in Greece; Establish a UN special committee to supervise foreign aid to Greece. Gromyko's speech was 10,000 words long and mostly repeated old tunes, such as accusing Greece's "fascist" government of implementing a policy of terror against domestic democratic and progressive elements. He also accused the United States of openly interfering in Greece's internal affairs, inciting the flames of civil war. The United States even held elections for the Greek government and wanted to make Greece enter into a state of economic and political slavery. Gromyko also warned the United States, declaring that if a solution could not be found in the UN General Assembly, adopting collective security action would cause the collapse of the UN organization and undermine genuine cooperation between nations. He said that the US's advocacy of open military intervention in Greece is an extremely unfavorable and dangerous path for the UN organization.

The British Conservative Party Strives to Make a Comeback; Churchill Condemns the Government and Launches a Major Attack on its Policy Towards the Soviet Union

[Reuters, Essex County, Snell's Brook, 27th] British wartime Prime Minister Churchill addressed 5,000 Conservative Party members here, severely attacking the Soviet Union's aggression and conspiracies, and its abuse of the veto power. He said: The United States today is facing militarized communism backed by Soviet military power, all because the Soviet government has launched aggressive conspiracies in the countries bordering it and the Soviet government has abused its veto power to undermine the UN organization, which the people of the world place great hope in.

Churchill also severely condemned the Labour government, pointing out the sharp decline in Britain's international standing, the decline in the people's living standards, and the ever-worsening domestic economic and financial situation. Churchill also mentioned the "Soviet Iron Curtain" speech he delivered in Fulton, Missouri, in the United States two years ago, saying that although the American people were surprised when they heard it at the time, if he were to give this speech again in the United States today, Americans would regard it as a stale argument with no stimulation. Churchill praised Foreign Secretary Bevin highly, saying that Bevin's firm diplomatic policy was in sharp contrast to what his other cabinet members were doing domestically. Here, Churchill again made a scathing criticism of socialism. He also called on Conservative Party members to prepare for a sudden election at any time so that they could be elected to represent a new opportunity for national strength and wisdom.

Churchill Comments on World Affairs

When commenting on recent major events in the world, Churchill pointed out that the execution of Bulgarian opposition leader Petkov was a judicial murder and a groundless murder, and said that the Soviet Union should bear the main responsibility for this matter. Churchill welcomed the government's decision to withdraw from Palestine, hoping that the withdrawal work could be carried out as quickly as possible. He pointed out that Britain was spending large sums of money and manpower in the Holy Land, and all it got was the resentment of the people there and around the world. He expressed his gratification that Britain was able to support the United States in maintaining the freedom and democracy of Europe and to provide food to famine-stricken countries. He also said that today he heard the cry of dollar panic for the first time, but it should be known that the dollar is the hard work of hundreds of millions of Americans, who voluntarily contribute, sometimes even without expecting repayment, to help the unfortunate people overseas. When talking about India, he said that the acts of slaughter there did not exceed his expectations, and this was just the beginning of an even worse situation in the future.

French Merchant Tram and Bus Services Did Not Resume Yesterday; British Merchant Tram Services Suddenly Went on Strike Again; Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Sternly Criticizes the Inaccuracy of the Cost of Living Index; Orders Resumption of Work or Consequential Action

[This newspaper's report] The labor strike of the French Merchant Water and Electricity Company's tram and bus workers has not been resolved. Some workers of the British Merchant Tram Company also entered a state of strike at 6:00 PM yesterday. All of the vehicles on Route 1, Route 2, Route 5, Route 3, Route 16, Route 14, Route 17, and Route 20 were successively driven into the depot and stopped around 7:00 PM. The routes of Route 8, Route 7, Route 10, and Route 11 still maintained service until the scheduled time. If the workers continue to be deadlocked, only the municipal Public Works Bureau's buses will serve the citizens today.

The French Merchant Electricity and Bus services remained suspended yesterday. More than 2,700 workers gathered in the union hall after the sit-down strike the day before yesterday afternoon, and only dispersed at 8:00 AM yesterday morning. At noon, the Social Affairs Bureau sent an official letter to the union, strictly ordering them to resume work on a specific date. The original letter stated: "It has been found that the chairman of the union, in order to demand bonus money and other issues, did not apply to this bureau according to law beforehand, and carried out a strike, which is incorrect. Now, at the time of the national general mobilization, workers must not strike or sit-down strike, and orders have been clearly issued. The union is to forward instructions to the striking workers to resume work on a specific date, in order to respect the law. If they dare to deliberately delay, it will be regarded as automatic resignation, and the company will be allowed to dismiss them unconditionally. The union bears the responsibility of leadership, and must earnestly guide them, and must not delay. This is extremely important, this order."

After receiving the instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau, the union announced to all workers that a temporary general meeting would be held at 4:00 PM to discuss the matter, but because not many people attended the meeting, there were no results. It was not until around 6:00 PM that the representatives of the ticket sales of Route 98 and the representatives of the line of Route 17 gave explanations to all the workers on behalf of the board of directors and supervisors, and decided to reconvene at 8:00 AM this morning to discuss the issue of resuming work.

[Da Gong News Agency] After the British Merchant Electricity and Bus workers went on strike, Wu Kaixian, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, said last night: This strike of the British Merchant trams is completely without reason. The union has always been unaware, and has not made any representations to the Social Affairs Bureau. Afterwards, a small number of workers stated that the reason for the strike was the inaccuracy of the cost of living index. The cost of living index investigated and compiled by the municipal authorities is absolutely accurate. Moreover, the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, which represents all the workers in the city, also conducted an index investigation in the middle of this month, and the figures compiled were roughly the same as those statistically compiled by the municipal bureau. This shows that the reasons they hold are merely excuses. Even if the index is inaccurate, the workers should first appeal to the government. The sudden strike shows that someone is instigating it from behind. The government authorities, considering that most of the good workers are being instigated, have limited them to resume work and hope that the workers will no longer be exploited by others, and will resume work soon, otherwise, they will have to take resolute measures, and will never tolerate it.

According to Qiu Changjiang, chairman of the British Merchant Tram Industry Union, the union had no knowledge of the reason for the suspension of British Merchant tram services last night. It was purely an external force that oppressed some of the workers and exploited them. After the outfield workers drove the vehicles into the military factory, they went home separately, so it was impossible to persuade them. It is still unknown whether work can be resumed today.

Various Parties Request the Selection and Appointment of Senators; City Council Sends Telegram to Central Authorities Urging Reconsideration

[Report from Our Newspaper] Last Friday (the 26th), during a State Council meeting,

a proposal was made by the Youth Party Committee of the Democratic Socialist Party to amend the regulations for city and county councils and provisional councils

to allow the central government to appoint representatives from various parties to participate in councils at all levels. The proposal has been passed and sent to the Legislative Yuan to be handled in accordance with the principles of the 12th article of the administrative policy. It is reported that the two speakers of the Shanghai Municipal Council, Pan and Xu, believe that any formal provincial, city, and county council generated by election should, in principle, not allow centrally appointed senators to participate midway, considering it a stain on democracy. Therefore, yesterday, in the name of the Municipal Council, they sent a telegram to the central government, requesting reconsideration, and also sent telegrams to all provincial and municipal councils, advocating for a unified stance. We are now transcribing their telegram to the

central authorities as follows:

To Chairman Jiang and Vice Chairman Sun of the Nanjing National Government,

President Sun and Vice President Wu of the Legislative Yuan, Premier Zhang and Vice Premier Wang of the Executive

Yuan, Your Excellencies: We have recently read in the newspapers of this city dated September 27th that the Democratic Socialist Party and the Youth Party Committee proposed on September 26th to amend the regulations for provincial, city, and county councils, intending

to request, in accordance with the principles of the 12th article of the administrative policy, that the Legislative Yuan amend the regulations for provincial, city, and county councils and provisional councils, using a selection method to

select representatives from various parties to jointly participate in provincial, city, and county councils or provisional councils. As for the number of representatives, it is proposed to be 15 to 20 people for provinces or municipalities directly under the central government, and 5 to 10 people for counties or cities under provincial jurisdiction. This proposal has been passed by the State Council and sent to the Legislative Yuan to be handled according to the original

principles. We are astonished upon reading this. We feel compelled to express our concerns: The regulations for the provincial, city, and county councils in our country have long been promulgated and implemented. The original proposal, based on the 12th article of the administrative policy, requests amendments, which contradicts the principle that laws should not be retroactive.

The Number of Appointed Representatives Hinders Civil Rights

Moreover,

all

provincial, city, and county

senators

are legally

elected by

various provincial, city, and county regional and professional groups according to

population proportions. Once the number of appointed senators is added midway, it directly and indirectly hinders

the exercise of the four rights of the people, treating national laws

as worthless and undermining the government's credibility. In fact,

regardless of provincial, city, and county councils,

the existing senators, although not proportionally allocated among various parties

or social elites, are definitely not limited to any single party. Taking Shanghai as an example, the number of senators with Kuomintang membership is less than 40 percent. Although it has not been investigated whether the Democratic Socialist Party and the Youth Party participate, it is evident that the remaining 60 percent are social elites or members of other parties.

Members of Both Parties Can Freely Compete in Elections

If selecting

provincial and municipal

supervisory

committee members,

there is originally

no restriction on party affiliation, and there is no need for senators to be candidates. Members of the Democratic Socialist Party and the Youth Party can continue to

compete freely through various methods, seemingly preventing

the issue of having no starting point. Moreover, the government implements

policies with the original intention of returning power to the people, not to

parties. Since the intention is to return power to the people, everything should

be based on the will of the people. Regarding the extension of the terms of the

senators, this is because provincial and municipal councils

will be established through legal elections.

It seems that members of the Democratic Socialist Party and the Youth Party should strive to promote

this, so that local councils can be

formed. Members of various parties can also participate in elections as soon as possible, realizing the goal of participating in local councils.

Established Regulations Cannot Be Altered

As for the

established

regulations of

provincial, city, and

county councils,

they should absolutely not

be easily altered. This council believes that the State Council

should carefully consider this matter. Besides sending telegrams to the

Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, and the National Government, and sending notifications to all provincial, city, and county councils to advocate for a unified stance, we hereby state that the regulations of provincial, city, and county councils should not cater to the demands of

party factions and increase the number of appointed representatives,

which would confuse them with those elected, causing

the government to appear to arbitrarily legislate and destroy laws, and to prioritize parties over the people.

We respectfully submit these reasons in a telegram for your review and hope that you will adopt and implement them, as it is in the public interest. President Pan Gongzhan of the Shanghai Municipal Council, Vice President Xu Ji,

respectfully submit this report.

Ordeal in the Barbaric Wilderness on the Border of Tuan Yan; Families of China National Aviation Corporation Crash Victims Recovered Nine Sets of Remains and Transported Them Back to Shanghai; Scattered and Incomplete Bones on the Slope

On March 19th of last year,

China National Aviation Corporation Flight 13

9, flying from Chongqing to

Shanghai, crashed en route.

The fate of the passengers and crew, totaling thirty-

six people, was unknown.

It was not until this summer that it was discovered that the crashed plane was located in the Zhong Zi area of "Tuan Yan." A month ago, the China National Aviation Corporation sent representatives and family members of the victims

to the location on a special plane to search for remains. They transported all the remains back to this city on a special plane, temporarily storing them in the China Funeral Home to prepare for the aftermath.

Yesterday, a reporter met Tao Chang, the representative of the families of the victims of the China National Aviation Corporation Flight 229, who provided the following account: This time, we and other representatives of the families of the China National Aviation Corporation Flight 229 crash victims went to Ebian County's Tuan Yan Mountain to search for remains. We departed from Shanghai on August 22nd, arrived in Chengdu on the 24th, and immediately contacted the provincial government authorities and relevant parties. Because entering the barbaric region was extremely difficult, it was necessary to complete negotiations. On September 4th, we set off for Ebian County.

At that time, western Sichuan was suffering from severe flooding, and the roads were destroyed. Military trucks could only reach Leshan. We then switched to rickshaws and walking, taking three days to reach Ebian County's

Shaping Town. Shaping is only 200 Chinese miles from the site of the Tuan Yan plane crash, but it requires passing through the "old forest," which is seldom visited.

There are many poisonous snakes and wild beasts,

and barbarians roam

the area, abducting people and selling them

as "slaves" to work. Therefore, Han Chinese have disappeared,

considering it a dreaded path. After we arrived at Shaping, we were

hosted by Mo Chengzhi, a local notable and current Sichuan provincial senator. His younger brother, Ge Chaolie,

planned everything for us. According to a report from a barbarian named Zhang Zhian last year, some passengers may still be alive,

having been abducted by barbarians. At that time, Ge placed an

announcement stating that if there were any survivors, he was willing

to offer a ransom for their release. Ge also sent someone to contact the chieftain of the barbarians, Mu Gan'er, explaining our

intentions to avoid misunderstandings. However, after a week,

there was no response. We then decided to bring guns and

venture forth,

led by Ge Chaowei

and a group of local people

and police officers, totaling sixty people. In addition to our family

representatives, there were also China National Aviation Corporation staff member Fan

Yuzhong, Mu Ye Company manager He Runzhi, and Ebian County police captain Xiao Qianxun,

carrying machine guns, submachine guns, rifles, and other weapons, totaling twenty-five

guns, in a group. In the "old forest,"

there were mostly cypress and fir trees, towering above the clouds, with bamboo lining the paths,

blocking out the sunlight. After traveling like this for three days, we

reached the border of Tuan Yan. As we approached the plane crash site, we suddenly saw several barbarians melting

the lead from the plane's wings. Seeing us, they shouted "

Chicken Pounced on the Ground," meaning that the barbarians wanted to tie people up,

and used

their barbarian knives to chop

at us fiercely. Another barbarian immediately

fired three shots, fortunately

missing. We immediately fired back and set up

the machine guns. Seeing that they were no match for us, the barbarians rolled

into the forest. At that time, a heavy fog filled the air, and they disappeared.

We then ordered people to guard the entrances while

rushing to the plane crash site to search for bodies

The plane crashed into a small rock on a flat dam,

and the bodies were scattered on the nearby slopes. Because it had been

so long, the bones were scattered and disorganized. We quickly collected them

at that time. Because we didn't know how many barbarians there were, fearing

that they would come again in force, we

quickly retreated

and rushed back to the

camp from the previous day to

ensure safety. The next day, we offered a generous reward,

gathering volunteers to search again. As a result, we only found

nine sets of remains, all incomplete. This was very different from the original

number of passengers. Because the time since the incident

was already a year and a half, the bodies were scattered and difficult

to collect.

Conspiracy to Sabotage Power; Police Bureau Offers Reward for Fugitive

The Municipal Police Bureau issued a public

subversives in this city were conspiring

to cause trouble, attempting to sabotage

power and create terror.

Previously, the Municipal Security Bureau seized important documents and arrested conspiracy offenders, including electrical worker

Wu Kewen and fourteen others. There are still fifteen fugitives, including Ouyang Zirun, who have not been captured.

It is reported that the police bureau has received a tip that the offenders not only do not regret their actions, but are also inciting

workers of the French Electric Tram Company and the British Electric Military Company to continue their strike in order to achieve their failed

objective. This is extremely illegal. We have ordered all subordinates to strictly arrest all the fugitives

and bring them to justice. A reward of ten million yuan will be offered for the arrest of Ouyang Zirun. For the arrest of the remaining fourteen people, including Li Yuanfu, Yang

Jinlong, Wang Yukun, Wan Shichang, Qian Shaohe, Li Zhensheng, Shen Xiangsheng, Wu Ze, Li Yi

tian, Ding Buyun, Yu Jiqing, Yang Yugen, Ni Renbao, and Liang Jinquan, each reward is five

million yuan. Half of the reward will be given to those who provide information leading to the arrest."

Celebration Turns to Tragedy; Collapse of Zhi Mei Lou Auditorium Injures Many

[Report from Our Newspaper] The Zhi Mei Lou Restaurant at 729 Hankou Road, across from the Yangzi Hotel, is owned by Yang De Tai. Recently, a large

building was newly built in the courtyard to serve as an auditorium for rent for weddings and funerals. Yesterday,

Sub-Bureau dispatched numerous police officers to investigate the truth and handle the matter.

Shanghai-Nanjing Express Train Separates; Delay Caused by Accident, Fortunately No Injuries

The 12th

Shanghai-Nanjing night express sleeper train departed

from Shanghai for Nanjing

at 11:00 PM. Yesterday,

at 0:35 AM,

when passing Zhengyi Station, the "Tiger Hook" connecting the fifth and sixth carriages behind the locomotive

suddenly broke due to the vibration. At that time, the train separated into two sections. The first half of the train did not notice the accident and continued

to travel. Fortunately, the train conductor managed to signal and stop the train. After Zhengyi Station dispatched a rescue train

to tow it back to the station, repairs were completed at 6:45 AM, resulting in a delay

of more than two hours. The other trains, such as Train 16, were also delayed as a result. Fortunately, there were no deaths or injuries.

Improving Agricultural Production and Increasing Exports to Overcome Current Economic Difficulties; Ge Jingzhong Speaks on "How China Can Achieve Economic Self-Reliance"

Mr. Ge Jingzhong During his Broadcast (Photo by Our Newspaper)

[Report from Our Newspaper] Yesterday, this newspaper held its 26th Sunday special broadcast at the Gospel Radio Station. Mr. Ge Jingzhong, General Manager of the China Silk Company, spoke on "How China Can Achieve Economic Self-Reliance." The main points of his speech are recorded below:

Recently, the Chinese economy has encountered many difficult

problems. Not only are we ourselves anxious, but our allied countries

are also extremely concerned. This can be seen from Wedemeyer's

report. At this difficult

time, we are putting forward the slogan of "self-reliance." The

so-called "self-reliance" is not intended to be isolationist.

International relations are now very close. We need to import

materials that we lack from other countries, and other countries also need

to export materials that they lack from our country. An isolationist policy can no longer adapt to

the current situation.

Self-Reliance to Regulate Trade

For example,

when the exchange rate

is high, prices also rise. When the exchange rate is low,

prices also fall. Also, China is an agricultural country.

To build it into an industrial country, we must purchase foreign

machinery. Therefore, when we talk about self-reliance now, it is about how to regulate our foreign trade,

which is about how to adjust exports and imports.

In short, it is about how to expand and increase our country's

exports in order to exchange for foreign imports, so that they can

be balanced. China is an agricultural country, and 80-90% of its products are agricultural products. Therefore, most of our exports

are tea, silk, tung oil, and pig bristles. Before the "September 18th Incident," soybeans were the top export. In 1937,

China's exports and imports were not very different. Unfortunately, the war broke out and lasted for eight years.

Export Quality Must Be Excellent

After

victory, we

also encountered domestic unrest. Therefore, there has been a huge trade deficit recently. The most tragic month last year,

the trade deficit reached 90%, meaning that exports were only worth 10% and imports were worth

100%. According to the latest customs announcement, the trade deficit is approximately 45%. On the surface, it seems that the situation has improved, but in reality,

because the use of foreign exchange is restricted, many luxurious or excessively valuable

items have been temporarily stopped from being imported. Some may ask, "Can we reduce imports and

balance them with exports?" This is impossible. When it comes to construction, it is essential to import machinery.

When there is a disaster, it is essential to import rice from Southeast Asia and cotton from India. Since reducing imports is impossible, we can only

try our best to expand exports. This raises the issue of quality and quantity.

The quality of exports must be excellent and scientific. For example, the tea leaves from Taiwan,

after scientific roasting, are very popular when shipped to the United States and Canada. If the Chinese mainland

were to use scientific methods for roasting, would the export of tea leaves not increase significantly?

Purchasing Agricultural Products while Considering Costs

Expanding

foreign trade

by improving quality is a fundamental solution,

but it is too slow. To solve the urgent problem, the quantity

must be increased. There is a simple method for this.

That is, the prices of products purchased from farmers must take their costs into account. For each agricultural product,

the labor, fertilizer, capital, and interest involved in the production process must be accurately calculated.

If we purchase materials from farmers based on these costs, they will naturally be happy

to sell, and without encouraging them to increase production, they will naturally increase production. If the purchase price does not cover the cost,

and we force them to sell, then the farmers would rather cut down the tea trees and mulberry trees to burn as firewood than do business at a loss.

Not Incurring Foreign Debt for Construction

Therefore,

if the

government wants to increase production and expand foreign trade, it must conduct a detailed investigation into the costs

of agricultural products. This is the most appropriate method and also a method for increasing quantity.

When foreign trade expands, we can exchange our

agricultural products for foreign industrial products. This way,

we can carry out construction without incurring foreign debt. This

is the true meaning of economic self-reliance. To realize

this true meaning, we must find ways to improve

the quality and quantity of our agricultural products, increase exports, and

overcome the current economic difficulties.

Shen Shuku's Ashes Scattered at Sea

Shen Shuku (Xin Gong), founder of the primary school attached to Nanyang Public School, dedicated himself to education for nearly thirty years. Unfortunately, he passed away on the 5th of this month. His wise son, following Shen's last wishes, had him cremated on September 7th at the Jing'an Temple Cemetery. At the request of his friends and classmates, a memorial service was held at the Moore Memorial Church on Tibet Road at 2:00 PM yesterday. Afterwards, the Shen family's ashes were placed in an ancient porcelain urn, and a special boat was chartered to the sea off Songkou. His wise son personally scattered the ashes into the sea from the starboard side. All the wreaths and flowers were also thrown into the sea. The sea burial ceremony concluded amidst the setting sun's rays reflecting on the clouds, waves, and mist.

Dance Industry Depressed, Restaurants Flourishing, Chicken and Duck Prices Soaring, Mooncakes Selling Well – Different Reactions to Thrift During the Festival

[Special Report from This Newspaper] After two emergency general meetings and three large-scale petitions by the city's dance industry, one dance hall manager said with a hint of loss, "Seeing the bright moon about to be full these past two days, our hearts are filled with indescribable sadness. Every year, from Mid-Autumn Festival to Christmas, is a golden period for the dance industry; now, just when everyone should be joyfully welcoming the Mid-Autumn Festival, we are struggling to overcome a crisis of survival!"

These words are quite melancholic. In the past month alone, they have abandoned the splendor and luxury they had painstakingly cultivated for over thirty years: neon lights dismantled, flower baskets disappeared, fragrant champagne no longer seen, and dazzling sterling silver utensils have begun to gather dust. The dance floors are indeed "thrifty" now, but what about outside the dance floors?

Fashion stores have autumn outfits costing nearly ten million yuan, and restaurants have lavish banquets costing two million yuan per table. Dance patrons and dancers, unable to enjoy themselves inside, naturally turn to these places as their ideal destinations. Restaurants are full of sea cucumbers and shark fins, aged Shaoxing wine, and Huadiao wine. If they want to indulge in intoxication, they can still feast to their heart's content, even though these are expressly restricted under the banner of thrift.

The "thrift" in the dance halls has unexpectedly led to the prosperity of restaurants, but this is limited to only thirty-odd larger restaurants. The more than seven hundred ordinary restaurants in the city are fearing the threat of "no tips allowed" brought about by the thrift campaign. The waiters in the restaurants that sell set meals are not paid a salary. What happens when their source of income from tips is cut off, leading to labor disputes?

The restaurant industry, generally speaking, is not interested in the Mid-Autumn Festival, which is the same melancholy shared by mooncake merchants. Last year, they had pagoda mooncakes and battleship mooncakes, magnificent and beautiful, decorating Shanghai with the joyous scene of family reunions. But times have changed, and a "Cloud Dress Fairy Moon" mooncake priced at 500,000 yuan stands alone in the city. Onlookers cannot help but feel disappointed, and oldtimers naturally feel even more shabby. Thus, they order their staff to put on smiling faces and explain apologetically to those who stop to look: "It's because we are complying with the price restrictions!" Finally, they add, "Next year, we will definitely make a huge, beautiful one!"

Whether customers are "inspired" by this kind of sales pitch is unknown, but people are frantically buying mooncakes, five boxes, ten boxes, coconut filling, jujube paste filling, the "mooncake mountain" piled on the counter gradually shrinking. One housewife-like customer anxiously says, "Hurry! I need to deliver these gifts today, or I'll be considered disrespectful tomorrow!"

Presumably, those receiving gifts are not practicing gratitude or refusal because of thrift, so the price of ducks has risen from 8,000 yuan to 24,000 yuan per catty. Pork has also doubled in price, and vegetables, oil, sugar, and the seven necessities of life have all increased in price. Everyone refuses to bow their heads to "thrift." Are they really prepared to hold on to their belts to enjoy the moon? In reality, most people are struggling to make ends meet. Are they just going through the motions for the holiday? Nine out of ten people giving gifts will solemnly say, "Because it's thrifty now, otherwise the gifts would have been even more elaborate!"

Those who are truly anxious about the thrift movement are the bands that play music at weddings, funerals, and celebrations, as well as many newly emerging artisans who make flower baskets and wreaths. They are all worried about their fate after the Mid-Autumn Festival. They once said with great emotion, "In the Qing Dynasty, even a low-ranking official of the seventh rank supported many idle people: sedan chair carriers, heralds, gate openers, cannon firers... These were professions passed down through generations. Later, when these duties were abolished, their entire families fell into despair!" The speaker meant to compare this to his current situation, but one of the listeners interrupted, "Those people did not all commit suicide or starve to death after their jobs were abolished. I have personally seen many of their descendants change professions and become wealthy!"

Everyone is busily spending the Mid-Autumn Festival, and the Mid-Autumn full moon will once again shine on these people – regardless of whether they are happy or sad!

Shen Bao

"Reader Scholarship Fund" Highest Individual Donation Record: Lu Shoulun Raises Funds, Yongyi Generously Donates 30 Million

Dear Readers,

If you are not forgetful, you will surely remember the enthusiastic support of Mr. Yongyi Guangsheng for scholarships in the past. This was already five years ago, when our motherland was under the enemy's iron heel, and the people were suffering in deep waters and hot fires, groaning in agony. In order to uphold the justice of the nation and for the future fate of the motherland, the "Reader Scholarship Fund" burst forth with brilliant sparks at that time, illuminating the future for the hesitant youth in the boundless darkness of enemy rule.

"As long as the stone is there, the spark will not die out." Countless enthusiastic people participated in our scholarship work, contributing money if they had it, and strength if they had it, and Mr. [Yongyi Guangsheng] was one of them.

Although the motherland's war of resistance has been won, the war against the communists has begun, and countless young people are still earnestly hoping for relief. Therefore, countless enthusiastic people have once again started scholarship work.

This time, Mr. [Yongyi Guangsheng] generously donated 30 million yuan, adding a new force to the "Reader Scholarship Fund". In terms of individual donations, Mr. [Yongyi Guangsheng] has undoubtedly broken the highest record again. Mr. [Yongyi Guangsheng] is a hardworking entrepreneur, a longtime reader of the Shen Bao. His career is both beneficial to the country and the people, and his diligence, simplicity, and benevolence are especially commendable.

Here, we would like to extend our highest gratitude to Mr. Yongyi and Mr. Lu (Note: It was Mr. Lu Shoulun who raised the funds) on behalf of countless poor and struggling students. (Editor's note) The famous Shanghai painter and calligrapher Feng Chaoran has specially created a landscape painting for us, and designated that this painting should be given to the person who donates the most money, to show our admiration and commemoration. Now that the "Reader Scholarship Fund" is nearing its end, the facts show us that this valuable landscape painting will be respectfully presented to Mr. Yongyi [Guangsheng]. I think readers must be very familiar with Mr. Feng's works. He has a lofty position in the art world, and Mr. Pan Gongzhan, the president of our newspaper, will add a postscript to it, adding a lot of luster to this painting. We believe that it is indeed a very honorable thing for a philanthropist like Mr. [Yongyi Guangsheng] to own this valuable work.
